# American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

## Chapter 13: U.S. Foreign Policy and Africa




### Introduction

The United States and Canada have a long history of diplomatic relations, dating back to the 18th century. Over the years, the two nations have developed a strong economic and political relationship, with both countries being major trading partners and allies. In this chapter, we will delve into the complexities of U.S. foreign policy towards Canada, examining the historical context, current state, and future prospects of this important relationship.

Throughout history, the United States and Canada have had a complex relationship, with periods of cooperation and conflict. The two nations share a border that stretches over 5,500 miles, and have a long history of trade and economic ties. However, there have also been periods of tension and disagreement, particularly over issues such as trade and immigration.

In recent years, the United States and Canada have worked to strengthen their relationship, with both nations recognizing the importance of cooperation in addressing global challenges. This includes issues such as climate change, border security, and economic growth. However, there are still areas of disagreement and potential conflict, such as the ongoing trade dispute between the two nations.

In this chapter, we will explore the history of U.S. foreign policy towards Canada, examining key events and developments that have shaped this relationship. We will also analyze current policies and initiatives, and discuss potential future developments and challenges. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the complexities of U.S. foreign policy towards Canada, and the impact it has on both nations and the global community.




### Subsection: 13.1 U.S.-Canada Trade Relations

The United States and Canada have a long history of trade relations, with a strong focus on energy trade. The two nations have a highly integrated energy relationship, with Canada being the largest foreign supplier of crude oil and natural gas to the United States. This relationship has been beneficial for both countries, with Canada providing a steady demand for its energy exports and the United States enhancing its energy security.

However, this relationship may be changing in the near future. With the growth of U.S. oil and natural gas production and reserves, the United States is no longer seen as an unlimited market for Canadian energy. This has led Canada to seek new export destinations, particularly in Asia. Both countries are also increasingly reliant on foreign investment to develop their resource sectors, with Asia serving as an important source of capital.

The expanding energy investment and trade between the United States and Canada have also led to increased economic ties between the two nations. In 2010, bilateral trade between the United States and Canada reached approximately $1.9 billion a day, making it one of the largest trading relationships in the world. This trade is essential for both countries, with the United States being Canada's largest trading partner and Canada being the United States' second-largest trading partner.

Despite the strong economic ties between the United States and Canada, there have been some challenges in their trade relationship. One of the main issues has been the trade imbalance between the two nations. In 2010, the United States had a trade deficit of $25.5 billion with Canada, meaning that the United States imported more goods from Canada than it exported. This has led to tensions between the two nations, with the United States pushing for more balanced trade.

To address this issue, the two nations have engaged in various trade agreements, such as the North American Free Trade Agreement (NAFTA) and the United States-Mexico-Canada Agreement (USMCA). These agreements aim to reduce trade barriers and promote fair and reciprocal trade between the United States and Canada. However, there have been some concerns about the impact of these agreements on certain industries, particularly in Canada.

In conclusion, the United States and Canada have a complex and intertwined trade relationship, with energy trade being a significant component. While there have been some challenges, both nations have worked to address them through various trade agreements. As the two nations continue to strengthen their economic ties, it will be interesting to see how their trade relationship evolves in the future.





### Subsection: 13.2 U.S.-Canada Security Cooperation

The United States and Canada have a long history of cooperation on security matters, with a focus on counterterrorism efforts and border security. This cooperation has been essential in addressing the shared threats and challenges faced by both nations.

#### Counterterrorism Efforts

The United States and Canada have a strong partnership in counterterrorism efforts, with a focus on intelligence sharing, joint training exercises, and coordinated responses to terrorist threats. This partnership has been particularly important in the aftermath of the 9/11 terrorist attacks, which highlighted the need for increased cooperation between the two nations.

One of the key areas of cooperation has been intelligence sharing. The United States and Canada have established various mechanisms for sharing intelligence, including the Canada-United States Intelligence Consultative Group (ICG) and the Five Eyes intelligence alliance. These mechanisms have allowed for the timely and effective sharing of information, leading to successful counterterrorism operations.

Joint training exercises have also been a crucial aspect of U.S.-Canada security cooperation. These exercises, such as the annual Maple Resolve exercises, allow for the practice of coordinated responses to terrorist threats and the testing of emergency response plans. They also provide an opportunity for the two nations to learn from each other and improve their capabilities.

#### Border Security

Border security has been a top priority for both the United States and Canada, with a focus on preventing illegal immigration and drug trafficking. The two nations have worked together to enhance border security, including the implementation of various technologies and the establishment of joint task forces.

One of the key areas of cooperation has been the use of technology, such as advanced surveillance systems and biometric identification. These technologies have allowed for more efficient and effective border control, leading to a decrease in illegal immigration and drug trafficking.

Joint task forces, such as the Canada-United States Joint Task Force West, have also been established to address specific border security issues. These task forces allow for the coordination of efforts and the sharing of resources, leading to more effective border security.

#### Conclusion

The United States and Canada have a strong partnership when it comes to security cooperation. This partnership has been essential in addressing the shared threats and challenges faced by both nations, and it continues to be a top priority for both governments. As the two nations face new and evolving security threats, this partnership will remain crucial in ensuring the safety and security of both nations.





### Subsection: 13.3a U.S.-Canada Cooperation on Climate Change

Climate change is a pressing global issue that requires international cooperation and action. The United States and Canada have a long history of cooperation on environmental issues, and climate change is no exception. Both nations have been signatories to the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change (UNFCCC) since its inception in 1992, and have been actively working together to address the impacts of climate change.

#### The International Joint Commission (IJC)

The International Joint Commission (IJC) is a key instrument of U.S.-Canada cooperation on environmental issues. Established in 1909 as part of the Boundary Waters Treaty, the IJC is responsible for resolving differences and promoting international cooperation on boundary waters. The IJC has been instrumental in addressing trans-border water pollution, most notably through the Great Lakes Water Quality Agreement of 1972.

#### The Air Quality Agreement of 1991

In 1986, the Canadian government of Brian Mulroney began pressing the Reagan administration for an "Acid Rain Treaty" to address U.S. industrial air pollution causing acid rain in Canada. The Reagan administration was hesitant, and questioned the science behind Mulroney's claims. However, Mulroney was able to prevail, and the product was the signing and ratification of the Air Quality Agreement of 1991 by the first Bush administration. Under this treaty, the two governments consult semi-annually on trans-border air pollution, which has demonstrably reduced acid rain. In 2000, an annex to the treaty was signed dealing with ground level ozone. Despite this, trans-border air pollution remains an issue, particularly in the Great Lakes-St. Lawrence watershed during the summer. The main source of this trans-border pollution results from coal-fired power stations, most of them located in the Midwestern United States.

#### The North American Agreement on Environmental Cooperation (NAAEC)

As part of the negotiations to create NAFTA, Canada and the U.S. signed, along with Mexico, the North American Agreement on Environmental Cooperation (NAAEC) in 1993. This agreement created the Commission for Environmental Cooperation (CEC), which monitors environmental issues across the continent, publishing the North American Environmental Atlas as one aspect of its monitoring duties. The CEC has been instrumental in promoting environmental cooperation and addressing shared environmental challenges, including climate change.

#### Current Efforts

Currently, both the United States and Canada are working towards meeting their commitments under the Paris Agreement on Climate Change. The U.S. has set a target to reduce its greenhouse gas emissions by 26-28% below its 2005 level by 2025, while Canada has committed to reducing its emissions by 30% below its 1990 level by 2030. Both nations have implemented various policies and initiatives to achieve these targets, including carbon pricing, renewable energy deployment, and energy efficiency measures.

In addition to these efforts, the U.S. and Canada have also been working together to address the impacts of climate change on their shared border. This includes efforts to protect and restore ecosystems, reduce air and water pollution, and promote sustainable development. The two nations have also been collaborating on research and technology development to advance clean energy solutions and mitigate the impacts of climate change.

Despite these efforts, there are still challenges and opportunities for further cooperation between the U.S. and Canada on climate change. These include addressing the impacts of climate change on indigenous communities, promoting sustainable resource management, and advancing clean technology innovation. As the impacts of climate change continue to intensify, it is crucial for the U.S. and Canada to continue working together to address this global issue.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between the United States and Canada in terms of foreign policy. We have seen how the two countries have a long history of cooperation and collaboration, but also how they have faced challenges and disagreements. From trade agreements to border security, the U.S. and Canada have a unique dynamic that is shaped by their geographical proximity and intertwined economies.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of communication and diplomacy in maintaining a strong relationship between these two nations. Despite their differences, the U.S. and Canada have been able to work together and find common ground through open dialogue and negotiation. This serves as a valuable lesson for other countries in navigating international relations.

Furthermore, we have also discussed the impact of U.S. foreign policy on Canada, particularly in terms of trade and security. The U.S. has been a major trading partner for Canada, and any changes in U.S. trade policies can have significant consequences for the Canadian economy. Similarly, the U.S. plays a crucial role in Canada's border security, and any changes in U.S. immigration policies can have a direct impact on Canada.

In conclusion, the relationship between the United States and Canada is complex and multifaceted, but it is also one of the most important in the world. The two nations have a shared history, intertwined economies, and a responsibility to work together to address global issues. By understanding the dynamics of this relationship, we can gain valuable insights into the intricacies of foreign policy and the importance of effective communication and diplomacy.

## Chapter: American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, the United States plays a crucial role in shaping international relations. As the world's largest economy and most powerful military, the U.S. has a significant impact on global politics and economics. One of the key aspects of U.S. foreign policy is its relationship with Latin America. The U.S. has a long history of involvement in Latin America, dating back to the 19th century when the U.S. expanded its territory through the acquisition of land from Spain and France. This chapter will provide a comprehensive analysis of U.S. foreign policy towards Latin America, examining the historical context, current policies, and future prospects.

The U.S. has a complex and often contentious relationship with Latin America. On one hand, the U.S. has been a major trading partner and investor in the region, providing economic support and aid. On the other hand, the U.S. has also been criticized for its interventionist policies and support for authoritarian regimes in Latin America. This chapter will delve into the various factors that have shaped U.S. foreign policy towards Latin America, including economic interests, security concerns, and ideological differences.

Furthermore, this chapter will also explore the impact of U.S. foreign policy on Latin America, examining the social, economic, and political consequences of U.S. involvement in the region. It will also discuss the challenges and opportunities for future cooperation between the U.S. and Latin America, including issues such as immigration, trade, and security. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of U.S. foreign policy towards Latin America and its implications for both regions.


# American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

### Subsection: 13.3b U.S.-Canada Cooperation on Water Management

Water management is a critical aspect of environmental cooperation between the United States and Canada. The two nations share a vast network of interconnected water bodies, including the Great Lakes, the St. Lawrence River, and the Mississippi River. These water bodies not only serve as vital sources of freshwater but also as important habitats for various species. Therefore, effective water management is crucial for the health and well-being of both nations.

#### The Great Lakes Water Quality Agreement of 1972

The Great Lakes Water Quality Agreement of 1972 is a landmark agreement between the United States and Canada that aims to protect and improve the water quality of the Great Lakes. The agreement was signed under the auspices of the International Joint Commission (IJC) and has been instrumental in addressing trans-border water pollution in the Great Lakes. The agreement has been updated several times, most recently in 2012, to address emerging issues such as climate change and invasive species.

#### The International Lake Stewardship Board

The International Lake Stewardship Board (ILSB) is a joint body of the United States and Canada that oversees the implementation of the Great Lakes Water Quality Agreement. The ILSB is responsible for setting water quality objectives, monitoring progress, and recommending actions to the IJC. The board is composed of experts from both nations and meets regularly to discuss and address issues related to water quality in the Great Lakes.

#### The Great Lakes Basin Water Quality Agreement

In addition to the Great Lakes Water Quality Agreement, the United States and Canada have also signed the Great Lakes Basin Water Quality Agreement. This agreement, signed in 1987, focuses on the protection and improvement of the water quality of the Great Lakes Basin, which includes not only the Great Lakes themselves but also the rivers, streams, and wetlands that feed into them. The agreement sets out a framework for cooperation between the two nations in managing the Basin's water resources.

#### The Great Lakes Restoration Initiative

In 2010, the United States and Canada launched the Great Lakes Restoration Initiative, a comprehensive plan to restore and protect the Great Lakes. The initiative includes actions to address invasive species, pollution, and habitat degradation, among other issues. The United States has committed $3 billion to the initiative, while Canada has contributed $1 billion. The initiative is a testament to the ongoing commitment of both nations to the protection and improvement of the Great Lakes.

In conclusion, water management is a critical aspect of U.S.-Canada environmental cooperation. The two nations have a long history of cooperation on water issues, and this cooperation continues to be a top priority in the 21st century.

### Conclusion

The relationship between the United States and Canada in terms of foreign policy has been a complex and multifaceted one. The two nations have been intertwined in various ways, from economic ties to cultural similarities. However, it is in the realm of foreign policy that the two nations have perhaps been most closely aligned. Both nations have been staunch supporters of democracy, human rights, and free trade, and have often found themselves on the same side of international issues.

The United States and Canada have also been close allies in terms of military and defense. The two nations have a long history of joint military exercises and training, and have been partners in various international conflicts. This close relationship has been a source of strength for both nations, and has helped to maintain stability in the region.

However, there have also been areas of disagreement between the United States and Canada in terms of foreign policy. The United States' decision to invade Iraq in 2003 was met with strong opposition from Canada, and the two nations have also had differing views on issues such as climate change and immigration.

Despite these differences, the overall relationship between the United States and Canada in terms of foreign policy has been one of cooperation and mutual respect. Both nations have been able to work together to address global issues and maintain stability in the region. As we move forward, it will be interesting to see how this relationship continues to evolve and shape the future of foreign policy in North America.

## Chapter: Chapter 14: U.S. Foreign Policy and Mexico

### Introduction

The United States and Mexico have a complex and intertwined history when it comes to foreign policy. The two nations share a border that spans over 1,900 miles, and their relationship has been shaped by a multitude of factors, including economic ties, immigration, and security concerns. In this chapter, we will delve into the intricacies of U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico, examining the historical context, current policies, and potential future developments.

The United States and Mexico have a long history of economic interdependence. The two nations have been trading partners for over a century, and today, Mexico is the United States' third-largest trading partner. This economic relationship has been a major factor in shaping U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico, with both nations heavily reliant on each other for economic growth.

However, the relationship between the two nations has not always been smooth. Immigration has been a contentious issue, with the United States often viewing Mexico as a source of illegal immigration. This has led to various policies and initiatives aimed at securing the border and deterring illegal immigration.

Security concerns have also played a significant role in U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico. The United States has provided significant military and financial aid to Mexico in an effort to combat drug trafficking and organized crime. However, some critics argue that these efforts have not been effective and have led to human rights abuses by Mexican security forces.

In this chapter, we will explore these issues and more, providing a comprehensive analysis of U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico. We will examine the historical context, current policies, and potential future developments, providing a deeper understanding of this complex and important relationship.




### Subsection: 13.3c U.S.-Canada Cooperation on Wildlife Conservation

Wildlife conservation is another critical aspect of environmental cooperation between the United States and Canada. Both nations are home to a diverse array of wildlife species, many of which are shared between the two countries. Therefore, effective wildlife conservation is crucial for the health and well-being of both nations.

#### The North American Waterfowl Management Plan

The North American Waterfowl Management Plan is a joint initiative between the United States, Canada, and Mexico that aims to protect and enhance waterfowl habitats across the continent. The plan was established in 1986 and has been instrumental in conserving and enhancing waterfowl habitats, particularly in the Prairie Pothole Region of North America.

#### Species Joint Ventures

Three species joint ventures currently exist under the North American Waterfowl Management Plan: the North American Waterfowl Management Plan, the Prairie Pothole Joint Venture, and the Arctic Coastal Plain Joint Venture. These joint ventures work to protect and enhance habitats for waterfowl species, such as the mallard, the Canada goose, and the snow goose.

#### Activities

By 2007, $827 million had been spent in Canada to purchase and enhance waterfowl habitats encompassing 4.4 million acres (18,000km). In total, joint ventures have invested $ 4.5 billion to protect 15.7 million acres (64,000km) of such habitats. The plan coordinates activities with other organizations, such as Ducks Unlimited, to protect and enhance waterfowl habitats.

#### Wildlife Conservation Society Canada

The Wildlife Conservation Society Canada (WCS Canada) is another important player in wildlife conservation in Canada. WCS Canada works to conserve wildlife and wild places in Canada and around the world. The organization has been instrumental in addressing issues such as white-nose syndrome (WNS), a disease that has "eradicated millions of bats in eastern North America." WCS Canada's Arctic research team has also been monitoring "ship noise and whale communications" for "potential impacts of increased ship traffic and noise" on whales and other marine mammals in the Northwest Passage.

#### Major Conservation Achievements

In 2018, WCS Canada improved tracking of wolverine populations through tagging in northern Ontario's boreal forest. They nurtured deep relationships with Indigenous Peoples in Canada to inform wildlife conservation projects "given the significant local knowledge" and "community-based monitoring". They worked with First Nations communities in Yukon and northern British Columbia by sharing WCS Canada's "expertise on conservation of fish and wildlife species to assist with the designing protected areas". In northern Ontario they worked with Moose Cree First Nation on a study of the "differences in lake sturgeon behavior in dammed and undammed rivers." They worked with Inuvialuit communities in the western Arctic, to "monitor seal health and diet as an indicator of the broader health of Arctic marine ecosystems." Scientists at Thompson Rivers University and McMaster University worked with WCS researchers to find solutions for white-nose syndrome (WNS). WNS has "eradicated millions of bats in eastern North America." The WCS Canada Arctic research team monitored "ship noise and whale communications" for "potential impacts of increased ship traffic and noise" on whales and other marine mammals in the Northwest Passage. WCS Canada's scientists worked on a "blueprint" for the proposed Bighorn Wildland Provincial Park which would protect important habitats for wildlife species.




### Conclusion

The relationship between the United States and Canada has been a complex and multifaceted one, shaped by a variety of factors including geography, history, and economic interdependence. In this chapter, we have explored the evolution of U.S. foreign policy towards Canada, examining the key events, policies, and personalities that have influenced this relationship.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of geography in shaping U.S. foreign policy towards Canada. The two countries' shared border and close proximity have led to a deep interdependence, with trade and security issues often taking center stage in their relationship. This has resulted in a complex web of policies and agreements, many of which have been shaped by the need to address these shared concerns.

Another important aspect of U.S. foreign policy towards Canada is the historical context. The two countries have a long history of cooperation and conflict, with the U.S. often playing a dominant role in Canadian affairs. This has led to a complex power dynamic between the two nations, with the U.S. often seen as a dominant force and Canada as a smaller, but still influential, player.

Economic interdependence has also played a significant role in shaping U.S. foreign policy towards Canada. The two countries have a strong economic relationship, with Canada being one of the U.S.'s largest trading partners. This has led to a deep economic integration, with many industries and businesses operating across the border. As a result, economic policies and agreements have been a key focus of U.S. foreign policy towards Canada.

In conclusion, the relationship between the United States and Canada is a complex and multifaceted one, shaped by a variety of factors. Geography, history, and economic interdependence have all played a significant role in shaping U.S. foreign policy towards Canada, and will continue to do so in the future.

## Chapter: American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

### Introduction

The United States and Mexico share a border that stretches over 1,900 miles, making it the longest international border in the world. This proximity has led to a deep interdependence between the two nations, with both countries heavily reliant on each other for trade, investment, and migration.

The United States has a long history of involvement in Mexico, dating back to the 19th century when the U.S. expanded its territory through the acquisition of land from Mexico. This history has left a lasting impact on the relationship between the two countries, with many issues still being contested today. One of the most contentious issues is the border wall, which has been a major focus of U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico.

In recent years, the U.S. has also faced challenges in addressing the growing issue of illegal immigration from Mexico. This has led to a complex and often controversial approach to immigration policy, with the U.S. implementing various measures such as deportations, border patrol, and guest worker programs. The impact of these policies on both countries has been significant, and we will explore the implications in this chapter.

These issues have had a profound impact on both countries and have been a major focus of U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico. We will examine the strategies and policies implemented by the U.S. to address these issues and their effectiveness.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive analysis of the complex relationship between the United States and Mexico. We will explore the historical context, current policies, and future prospects of this relationship, shedding light on the intricate dynamics between these two neighboring nations.

## Chapter: American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will delve into the complex relationship between the United States and Mexico, two neighboring countries with a long history of intertwined political, economic, and cultural ties. The United States and Mexico share a border that stretches over 1,900 miles, making it the longest international border in the world. This proximity has led to a deep interdependence between the two nations, with both countries heavily reliant on each other for trade, investment, and migration.

The United States has a long history of involvement in Mexico, dating back to the 19th century when the U.S. expanded its territory through the acquisition of land from Mexico. This history has left a lasting impact on the relationship between the two countries, with many issues still being contested today. One of the most contentious issues is the border wall, which has been a major focus of U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico.

In recent years, the U.S. has also faced challenges in addressing the growing issue of illegal immigration from Mexico. This has led to a complex and often controversial approach to immigration policy, with the U.S. implementing various measures such as deportations, border patrol, and guest worker programs. The impact of these policies on both countries has been significant, and we will explore the implications in this chapter.

## Chapter 1:4: U.S. Foreign Policy and Mexico:




### Introduction

The relationship between the United States and Mexico has been a complex and often contentious one. The two countries share a long and intertwined history, with deep cultural, economic, and political ties. However, this relationship has also been marked by periods of tension and conflict, particularly in the realm of foreign policy. In this chapter, we will delve into the intricacies of U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico, examining the historical context, key events, and current state of affairs.

We will begin by exploring the historical foundations of this relationship, tracing the origins of U.S. involvement in Mexico and the impact of various policies and interventions over time. This will include a discussion of the Mexican-American War, the U.S. acquisition of Texas and California, and the subsequent establishment of the U.S.-Mexico border.

Next, we will examine the economic aspects of this relationship, including the impact of trade agreements and immigration policies on both countries. We will also explore the role of Mexico as a key trading partner and source of labor for the U.S., and the challenges and opportunities this presents for both nations.

Finally, we will delve into the current state of U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico, including the ongoing issues of immigration, drug trafficking, and security concerns. We will also discuss the efforts of both countries to address these issues and the potential for future cooperation and collaboration.

Through this comprehensive analysis, we aim to provide a deeper understanding of the complex dynamics of U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico, shedding light on the historical, economic, and political factors that have shaped this relationship. By examining the past, present, and future of this relationship, we hope to gain valuable insights into the role of the U.S. in Mexico and the impact of its policies on both nations and the wider region.




### Subsection: 14.1 U.S.-Mexico Trade Relations

The United States and Mexico have a complex and intertwined trade relationship, with both countries heavily reliant on each other for economic growth and development. In this section, we will explore the history of U.S.-Mexico trade relations, the current state of trade between the two nations, and the impact of trade on their overall relationship.

#### Historical Context

The United States and Mexico have a long history of trade relations, dating back to the 19th century when the U.S. established trade agreements with Mexico. However, it was not until the 1990s that trade between the two nations truly began to flourish. In 1997, the two countries signed the North American Free Trade Agreement (NAFTA), which eliminated tariffs and other trade barriers between the U.S., Mexico, and Canada. This agreement has had a significant impact on the trade relationship between the U.S. and Mexico, with trade between the two nations increasing by over 500% since its implementation.

#### Current State of Trade

Today, the U.S. and Mexico have one of the largest trading relationships in the world, with two-way trade reaching over $1 billion in 2018. Mexico is the United States' third-largest trading partner, and the U.S. is Mexico's second-largest trading partner. The two nations have a diverse range of trade, with the U.S. exporting goods such as machinery, electronics, and chemicals to Mexico, and Mexico exporting goods such as vehicles, oil, and agricultural products to the U.S.

#### Impact of Trade

The trade relationship between the U.S. and Mexico has had a significant impact on both nations' economies. In the U.S., trade with Mexico supports over 1.7 million jobs, and the two nations have a combined trade surplus of over $80 billion. In Mexico, trade with the U.S. has led to economic growth and development, with the country's GDP increasing by over 60% since the implementation of NAFTA.

However, the trade relationship has also faced challenges, particularly in regards to immigration and labor practices. The U.S. has raised concerns about the lack of labor protections in Mexico, leading to the exploitation of workers and the importation of goods produced by forced labor. In response, the U.S. has implemented the Generalized System of Preferences (GSP) to promote fair labor practices in Mexico and other developing countries.

#### Future of Trade

The U.S. and Mexico have a complex and intertwined trade relationship, with both nations heavily reliant on each other for economic growth and development. As the two nations continue to navigate their trade relationship, it is essential to address any concerns and work towards a mutually beneficial agreement that promotes fair labor practices and economic growth. The future of U.S.-Mexico trade relations will continue to shape the relationship between these two neighboring nations.





### Subsection: 14.2 U.S.-Mexico Security Cooperation

The United States and Mexico have a complex and often contentious relationship when it comes to security cooperation. The two nations share a long border, with over 1,900 miles of it being undeveloped and remote, making it difficult for the U.S. to monitor and control illegal activity. This has led to a significant issue with illegal immigration, drug trafficking, and other forms of transnational crime.

#### Historical Context

The U.S. and Mexico have a long history of security cooperation, with the two nations working together to address issues such as drug trafficking and illegal immigration. However, this cooperation has often been strained due to differing priorities and approaches. For example, the U.S. has historically focused on addressing drug trafficking and illegal immigration at the border, while Mexico has prioritized addressing these issues within its own borders.

#### Current State of Security Cooperation

Today, the U.S. and Mexico continue to work together to address security issues, but there have been significant changes in their approach. The U.S. has shifted its focus from solely addressing issues at the border to also addressing them within Mexico. This has led to increased cooperation and information sharing between the two nations.

One example of this is the Merida Initiative, a bilateral security cooperation agreement between the U.S. and Mexico that was established in 2007. This initiative has provided over $3 billion in military and law enforcement aid to Mexico, with the goal of addressing drug trafficking, illegal immigration, and other forms of transnational crime.

#### Impact of Security Cooperation

The increased security cooperation between the U.S. and Mexico has had a significant impact on both nations. In the U.S., it has led to a decrease in illegal immigration and drug trafficking, with the number of illegal border crossings dropping by over 80% since 2000. In Mexico, it has helped to disrupt and dismantle drug trafficking organizations, leading to a decrease in drug-related violence.

However, there have also been criticisms of this increased cooperation. Some argue that it has led to human rights abuses by Mexican security forces, while others argue that it has not been effective in addressing the root causes of illegal immigration and drug trafficking.

Despite these criticisms, security cooperation between the U.S. and Mexico remains a top priority for both nations. As the two nations continue to work together, it is important to address these issues and find a balance that benefits both nations while also respecting their sovereignty.





### Subsection: 14.3a U.S. Border Wall and Mexico

The issue of a border wall between the United States and Mexico has been a contentious topic in U.S. foreign policy for decades. It has been a key campaign promise of many U.S. presidential candidates, and has been a major point of contention between the U.S. and Mexico.

#### Historical Context

The idea of a border wall between the U.S. and Mexico dates back to the 19th century, when the U.S. and Mexico were engaged in territorial disputes. The U.S. ultimately acquired the land that is now the southwestern United States from Mexico in the Mexican-American War of 1846-1848. Since then, there have been efforts to secure the border, including the construction of physical barriers such as fences and walls.

In recent years, the issue of a border wall has become more prominent due to the increasing concern over illegal immigration and drug trafficking. The U.S. has spent billions of dollars on border security, including the construction of physical barriers, but the issue remains a major concern for both nations.

#### Current State of the Border Wall

Today, the U.S. and Mexico share a border that is over 1,900 miles long. The existing MexicoUnited States barrier is not one continuous structure, but a series of physical walls and physical and "virtual" fences monitored by the United States Border Patrol. The proposed wall, which was a key campaign promise of President Donald Trump, would be a "contiguous, physical wall or other similarly secure, contiguous, and impassable physical barrier" along the entire length of the border.

President Trump signed an executive order in January 2017 calling for the construction of a border wall, and in April 2017, the Department of Homeland Security released a request for proposals for border wall prototypes. However, the construction of the wall has faced numerous challenges, including legal challenges and funding issues.

#### Impact of the Border Wall

The proposed border wall has had a significant impact on the relationship between the U.S. and Mexico. Mexico has strongly opposed the construction of a border wall, with Mexican President Enrique Pea Nieto stating that his country will not pay for the wall. This has led to tension between the two nations, with the U.S. threatening to withhold aid and impose tariffs on Mexican imports.

The proposed border wall has also faced criticism from within the U.S., with many arguing that it is an ineffective and expensive solution to the issue of illegal immigration and drug trafficking. Others argue that it is a symbol of division and hostility towards Mexico, and could have negative consequences for the relationship between the two nations.

Despite these challenges, President Trump remains committed to the construction of a border wall, and it remains a key issue in U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico. The future of the border wall remains uncertain, but it is clear that it will continue to be a contentious topic in the U.S.-Mexico relationship.





### Subsection: 14.3b U.S. Deportation Policy and Mexico

The issue of deportation has been a contentious topic in U.S. foreign policy, particularly in relation to Mexico. Deportation is the process of removing a non-citizen from a country, and it has been a key tool in the U.S.'s immigration enforcement efforts. However, the impact of deportation on Mexico has been a major concern for both nations.

#### Historical Context

Deportation has been a part of U.S. immigration law since the early 20th century. The Immigration and Nationality Act of 1952, also known as the McCarran-Walter Act, established the current framework for deportation in the U.S. The act allows for the deportation of non-citizens who are convicted of certain crimes, have been in the U.S. illegally for more than 180 days, or have been deemed a threat to national security.

#### Current Deportation Policy

Today, the U.S. deports an average of 1,000 people per day, with the majority of those deportations occurring at the U.S.-Mexico border. The U.S. has also entered into agreements with Mexico to accept the return of Mexican nationals who are deported from the U.S. This has led to a significant increase in the number of deportations from the U.S. to Mexico.

#### Impact of Deportation on Mexico

The high rate of deportations from the U.S. to Mexico has had a significant impact on Mexico. Many deportees return to Mexico with limited resources and face challenges in reintegrating into society. This has led to an increase in poverty and social issues in Mexico, particularly in border communities.

Furthermore, the U.S.'s deportation policy has also had a ripple effect on Mexico's own immigration policies. In response to the high number of deportations, Mexico has implemented stricter immigration policies and increased border security. This has led to a decrease in the number of Mexican nationals seeking asylum in the U.S., but has also resulted in the detention and deportation of more Central American migrants.

#### U.S.-Mexico Cooperation on Deportation

The U.S. and Mexico have a complex relationship when it comes to deportation. While the U.S. has been a major source of deportees for Mexico, the two nations have also worked together to address the issue. In 2016, the U.S. and Mexico signed an agreement to address the root causes of migration and to increase cooperation on immigration enforcement. This agreement has led to increased communication and information sharing between the two nations, as well as joint efforts to address the issue of deportation.

In conclusion, the U.S.'s deportation policy has had a significant impact on Mexico, both in terms of the number of deportees and the resulting social and economic challenges. However, the two nations have also worked together to address the issue, demonstrating the complex and often intertwined nature of U.S.-Mexico relations.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between the United States and Mexico. We have examined the historical context of this relationship, including the impact of colonialism, the Mexican-American War, and the Bracero Program. We have also delved into the current state of affairs, discussing issues such as immigration, trade, and security. Through this comprehensive analysis, we have gained a deeper understanding of the dynamics at play in this important bilateral relationship.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of understanding the historical context in which current events occur. By examining the long history of U.S.-Mexico relations, we can better understand the underlying factors that shape current policies and decisions. This is crucial in navigating the complexities of this relationship and finding effective solutions to the challenges that arise.

Another important aspect to consider is the impact of U.S. foreign policy on Mexico. As the United States is a dominant global power, its actions have a significant impact on its neighbor to the south. This is evident in issues such as immigration, where U.S. policies have played a major role in driving migration from Mexico. It is crucial for the United States to consider the potential consequences of its actions on Mexico and to engage in a more collaborative and mutually beneficial relationship.

In conclusion, the United States and Mexico have a complex and intertwined relationship that has shaped the political, economic, and social landscapes of both nations. By understanding the historical context and the impact of U.S. foreign policy, we can better navigate this relationship and work towards a more cooperative and mutually beneficial future.

The United States, with its history of colonialism and expansion, has had a significant impact on Canada's foreign policy. This chapter will explore the historical context of this relationship, as well as the current state of affairs between the two nations.

The United States and Canada share a long border, with over 1,500 miles of land and water boundaries. This proximity has led to a close economic relationship, with both nations heavily reliant on each other for trade. However, this economic relationship has also been a source of tension, particularly in regards to trade policies and tariffs.

Furthermore, the United States and Canada have a complex history of diplomatic relations. The two nations have been allies since the 19th century, but this alliance has not been without its challenges. The United States has often been criticized for its interventionist foreign policy, which has had a direct impact on Canada's foreign policy decisions.

In this chapter, we will also examine the role of Canada in shaping American foreign policy. As a neighboring country, Canada has been a key player in influencing U.S. policies, particularly in regards to trade and security. We will also discuss the impact of Canada's foreign policy on its own domestic affairs, including issues of immigration and national identity.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive analysis of the relationship between the United States and Canada, highlighting the complexities and nuances of this important bilateral relationship. By examining the historical context and current state of affairs, we hope to gain a deeper understanding of the dynamics at play in this crucial relationship.


# American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

## Chapter 15: U.S. Foreign Policy and Canada




### Subsection: 14.3c U.S. Asylum Policy and Mexico

The issue of asylum has been a major point of contention in U.S. foreign policy, particularly in relation to Mexico. Asylum is a form of protection granted to individuals who fear persecution in their home country on account of race, religion, nationality, membership in a particular social group, or political opinion. The U.S. has a long history of providing asylum to individuals fleeing persecution, but recent policies have raised concerns about the treatment of asylum seekers and the impact on Mexico.

#### Historical Context

The U.S. has a long history of providing asylum to individuals fleeing persecution. The 1967 United Nations Protocol Relating to the Status of Refugees, also known as the 1967 Refugee Convention, established the current framework for asylum in the U.S. The protocol defines a refugee as a person who is outside their country of origin and is unable or unwilling to return due to a well-founded fear of being persecuted for reasons of race, religion, nationality, membership of a particular social group, or political opinion.

#### Current Asylum Policy

In recent years, the U.S. has implemented several policies that have restricted the ability of individuals to seek asylum. In June 2018, the Department of Justice implemented a policy to deny that lack of protection from gender-based violence or gang violence were lawful bases for claiming asylum. This policy was overturned by a federal judge in December 2018, but it has had a significant impact on the ability of individuals to seek asylum in the U.S.

In November 2018, President Trump issued a proclamation suspending the right of asylum to any migrant crossing the USMexico border outside of a lawful port of entry. This policy was met with legal challenges and was ultimately overturned by the U.S. Supreme Court in December 2018. However, the U.S. has continued to implement policies that make it more difficult for individuals to seek asylum, such as the Migrant Protection Protocols, colloquially known as the "Remain in Mexico" program, which allows the government to release migrants with asylum claims to Mexico to await their asylum hearings in the United States.

#### Impact of U.S. Asylum Policy on Mexico

The U.S.'s asylum policy has had a significant impact on Mexico. As the U.S. has become less welcoming to asylum seekers, more individuals have been forced to seek asylum in Mexico. This has put a strain on Mexico's resources and has led to an increase in the number of migrants in Mexico, many of whom are living in dangerous and overcrowded conditions.

Furthermore, the U.S.'s asylum policy has also had a ripple effect on Mexico's own immigration policies. In response to the high number of Central American migrants seeking asylum in the U.S., Mexico has implemented stricter immigration policies and increased border security. This has led to a decrease in the number of Central American migrants seeking asylum in the U.S., but has also resulted in the detention and deportation of more Central American migrants from Mexico.

In conclusion, the U.S.'s asylum policy has had a significant impact on Mexico, both in terms of the treatment of asylum seekers and the impact on Mexico's own immigration policies. As the U.S. continues to grapple with its asylum policy, it is important to consider the impact on Mexico and work towards a more humane and effective solution for both nations.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between the United States and Mexico, and how it has shaped American foreign policy. We have discussed the historical context of this relationship, including the impact of colonialism, immigration, and trade. We have also examined the current state of affairs, including the challenges of drug trafficking, illegal immigration, and economic disparities. Through this analysis, we have gained a deeper understanding of the complexities and nuances of U.S.-Mexico relations and how it has influenced American foreign policy.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of understanding the historical and cultural factors that have shaped this relationship. By acknowledging the complexities of this relationship, we can better understand the motivations and actions of both the United States and Mexico. This understanding is crucial in developing effective foreign policy strategies that address the root causes of issues such as drug trafficking and illegal immigration.

Another important aspect to consider is the impact of U.S.-Mexico relations on other countries in the region. As we have seen, the decisions made by the United States and Mexico have far-reaching consequences for neighboring countries. It is essential for American foreign policy to take into account the potential ripple effects of its actions on other nations.

In conclusion, the relationship between the United States and Mexico is a complex and ever-evolving one. By understanding the historical, cultural, and economic factors that have shaped this relationship, we can develop more effective foreign policy strategies that address the challenges and opportunities presented by this relationship.

### Conclusion

The relationship between the United States and Mexico has been a complex and often contentious one. From the early days of colonization and territorial expansion, to the modern issues of immigration and trade, the two nations have been intertwined in both positive and negative ways. In this chapter, we have explored the history of U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico, examining the various factors that have influenced this relationship and the impact it has had on both nations.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of understanding the historical context of U.S.-Mexico relations. From the Mexican-American War to the NAFTA agreement, the decisions made by the United States have had a profound impact on Mexico and its people. It is crucial for policymakers and scholars to consider this history when making decisions about U.S. foreign policy towards Mexico.

Another important aspect to consider is the role of immigration in this relationship. The United States has a long history of immigration, and Mexico has been a major source of immigrants. However, the treatment of Mexican immigrants has often been a contentious issue, with policies such as the Bracero Program and the current border wall being examples of the complex dynamics at play. It is important for policymakers to address these issues in a fair and just manner, taking into account the historical and cultural context of the relationship.

In addition to immigration, trade has also played a significant role in U.S.-Mexico relations. The NAFTA agreement has had a profound impact on both nations, with some arguing that it has led to job losses and economic instability in Mexico. It is important for policymakers to carefully consider the potential consequences of trade agreements and to work towards mutually beneficial agreements that benefit both nations.

Overall, the relationship between the United States and Mexico is a complex and multifaceted one, with a long history of influence and impact. It is crucial for policymakers and scholars to continue studying and analyzing this relationship in order to make informed decisions and work towards a more positive and mutually beneficial future.

# American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

## Chapter 15: U.S. Foreign Policy and Canada




### Introduction

The relationship between the United States and Russia has been a topic of great interest and debate for decades. Both countries have played significant roles in global affairs, and their interactions have had a profound impact on the world stage. In this chapter, we will delve into the complex dynamics of U.S. foreign policy towards Russia, examining the historical context, key events, and current state of affairs.

The United States and Russia have a long history of diplomatic relations, dating back to the 19th century. However, their relationship has been marked by periods of tension and conflict, particularly during the Cold War era. The two superpowers engaged in a race for global influence, with the United States representing the Western world and Russia leading the Eastern bloc. This rivalry was characterized by political, economic, and military competition, often playing out on the world stage.

Since the collapse of the Soviet Union in 1991, the United States has been the sole superpower, and its foreign policy towards Russia has been shaped by this new reality. The U.S. has sought to promote its interests and values while also managing potential threats posed by Russia. This has led to a complex and often contentious relationship, with both countries vying for influence in various global hotspots.

In this chapter, we will explore the key factors that have shaped U.S. foreign policy towards Russia, including historical events, political ideologies, and economic interests. We will also examine the current state of affairs between the two countries, including areas of cooperation and conflict. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the complex dynamics of U.S. foreign policy towards Russia and its impact on the global stage.




### Subsection: 15.1 U.S.-Russia Arms Control

The relationship between the United States and Russia has been marked by a complex interplay of arms control agreements and violations. These agreements have been a crucial aspect of U.S.-Russia relations, serving as a means of managing and reducing the threat of nuclear weapons. However, recent developments have raised concerns about the future of these agreements and their effectiveness in preventing the proliferation of weapons of mass destruction.

#### The New START Treaty

The New Strategic Arms Reduction Treaty (New START) is a bilateral agreement between the United States and Russia, signed in 2010, that limits the number of deployed strategic warheads to 1,550 for each country. This agreement also includes verification measures, such as on-site inspections, to ensure compliance. The New START is set to expire in 2026, and there have been ongoing discussions about its extension.

The New START has been a crucial tool in managing the U.S.-Russia arms race. It has led to a significant reduction in the number of deployed strategic warheads, from 2,200 to 1,550, and has also allowed for greater transparency and verification measures. However, there have been concerns about Russian compliance with the treaty, particularly in regards to the development of new weapons systems.

#### Russian Compliance with the New START

Russia has been accused of violating the New START treaty through its development of new weapons systems, such as the RS-28 Sarmat and the Status-6 Ocean Multipurpose System. These weapons are not covered by the New START, leading to concerns about Russian non-compliance. Additionally, there have been reports of Russian cheating on the treaty, such as the alleged movement of nuclear warheads between different types of missiles.

The U.S. has also raised concerns about Russian compliance with the New START in regards to the number of deployed strategic warheads. The Federation of American Scientists estimates that Russia has 5,977 nuclear weapons, while the U.S. has 5,428. This discrepancy raises questions about the accuracy of Russian reporting and compliance with the treaty.

#### The Future of U.S.-Russia Arms Control

The future of U.S.-Russia arms control is uncertain. The New START is set to expire in 2026, and there have been ongoing discussions about its extension. However, the U.S. has also expressed concerns about the effectiveness of the treaty in preventing the proliferation of weapons of mass destruction. The development of new weapons systems by Russia, such as the RS-28 Sarmat and the Status-6 Ocean Multipurpose System, has raised concerns about the future of arms control agreements between the two countries.

In conclusion, the U.S.-Russia arms control relationship has been marked by a complex interplay of agreements and violations. The New START has been a crucial tool in managing the arms race between the two countries, but concerns about Russian compliance have raised questions about its effectiveness. The future of U.S.-Russia arms control is uncertain, and it is essential for both countries to work towards a mutually beneficial solution to prevent the proliferation of weapons of mass destruction.





### Subsection: 15.2 U.S.-Russia Economic Relations

The economic relationship between the United States and Russia has been complex and often strained. While the two countries have engaged in significant trade, their political differences have often overshadowed their economic ties. In recent years, the relationship has been further complicated by the annexation of Crimea and the ongoing conflict in Ukraine.

#### U.S.-Russia Trade Relations

Despite the political tensions between the two countries, the United States and Russia have engaged in significant trade. In 2018, the total trade between the two countries amounted to $25.9 billion, with the United States exporting $11.6 billion worth of goods and services to Russia and importing $14.3 billion worth of goods and services from Russia. The top U.S. exports to Russia include machinery, aircraft, and pharmaceuticals, while the top Russian exports to the United States include oil, metals, and chemicals.

However, the trade relationship between the two countries has been marked by significant imbalances. In 2018, the United States had a trade deficit of $2.7 billion with Russia, meaning that the United States imported more goods and services from Russia than it exported. This trade imbalance has been a source of contention in the economic relationship between the two countries.

#### U.S. Sanctions on Russia

In response to Russia's annexation of Crimea and its involvement in the ongoing conflict in Ukraine, the United States has imposed a series of economic sanctions on Russia. These sanctions aim to put pressure on the Russian government and its economy, and are designed to limit Russia's ability to access the global financial system and engage in international trade.

The sanctions have had a significant impact on the Russian economy, leading to a decline in foreign investment and a decrease in the value of the Russian ruble. However, they have also had unintended consequences, such as driving Russia closer to China and other emerging markets.

#### U.S.-Russia Economic Relations in the Context of the New START

The New START treaty, signed in 2010, has played a role in the economic relationship between the United States and Russia. The treaty has led to a reduction in the number of deployed strategic warheads, which has had a positive impact on global security. However, concerns have been raised about Russian compliance with the treaty, particularly in regards to the development of new weapons systems.

The ongoing economic relationship between the United States and Russia, despite political tensions, highlights the complex nature of their relationship. While economic ties have been strained, they continue to play a role in the overall relationship between the two countries. As the New START treaty approaches its expiration date in 2026, it will be important for both countries to continue to engage in dialogue and work towards a mutually beneficial agreement.





### Subsection: 15.3a U.S. Sanctions on Russia for Cyber Attacks

In recent years, the United States has also imposed sanctions on Russia for its malicious cyber activities. These sanctions are designed to hold Russia accountable for its cyber attacks and to deter future attacks.

#### U.S. Sanctions on Russia for Cyber Attacks

The United States has imposed sanctions on Russia for a variety of cyber attacks, including those targeting critical infrastructure, financial institutions, and political organizations. These sanctions are imposed under the authority of the Treasury's Office of Foreign Assets Control (OFAC), which is responsible for enforcing economic sanctions.

One of the key pieces of legislation that enables these sanctions is the Countering America's Adversaries Through Sanctions Act (CAATSA). This law, passed in 2017, provides the legal authority for the United States to impose sanctions on individuals and entities involved in cyber attacks against the United States.

#### Impact of U.S. Sanctions on Russia for Cyber Attacks

The impact of these sanctions on Russia has been significant. The sanctions have targeted key individuals and entities involved in cyber attacks, including former Russian intelligence chief Mikhail Fradkov, who was sanctioned in 2018. These sanctions have also targeted Russian cybersecurity firms and individuals involved in cyber espionage.

The sanctions have also had a broader impact on the Russian economy. As with other economic sanctions, the cyber sanctions have contributed to a decline in foreign investment and a decrease in the value of the Russian ruble. This has put further pressure on the Russian economy, which is already struggling under the weight of international sanctions imposed in response to the annexation of Crimea and the ongoing conflict in Ukraine.

#### Future of U.S. Sanctions on Russia for Cyber Attacks

The future of U.S. sanctions on Russia for cyber attacks is promising. The developments on legalizing the cyber sanctions in the United States are promising that we might see enactment of more bills focusing on cyber issues at the international level. As of now, there are two executive orders (Executive Order 13694 and Executive Order 13757) that explains how malicious cyber activities will be replied with the use of economic sanctions and other measures. The authority of the Treasury's Office of Foreign Assets Control (OFAC) is responsible for the initiation and outcomes of the economic sanctions related to cyber-related activities.

The European Union has also taken steps to enhance collective cyber response, focusing on sanctioning the target by creating a new entity, which is called cyber intelligence working group. Although there are steps taken in using economic sanctions for cyber-related attacks against the EU, these measures are still in their early stages and there is much work to be done.




### Subsection: 15.3b U.S.-Russia Cooperation on Cybersecurity

The United States and Russia have a complex relationship when it comes to cybersecurity. While there have been instances of cyber attacks and espionage between the two nations, there have also been instances of cooperation and information sharing. This section will explore the history of U.S.-Russia cooperation on cybersecurity, including notable instances of cooperation and the challenges that have arisen.

#### Notable Instances of U.S.-Russia Cooperation on Cybersecurity

One notable instance of U.S.-Russia cooperation on cybersecurity is the U.S.-China Arms Control Technical Exchange Program (ACE). This program, created in 1994, brings together nuclear scientists from major weapon labs such as Los Alamos National Laboratory and China's Academy of Engineering Physics (CAEP) to work together on nuclear security issues. This program has been instrumental in addressing nuclear security issues around the world, including in Iran and Ghana.

Another notable instance of cooperation is the U.S.-China Law Enforcement and Cyber Security Dialogue. This dialogue, established in 2017, allows both countries to work together to address problems with hacking and improve global computer security and cyber-security. This dialogue has been particularly important in addressing cyber threats that cross national borders, such as cyber espionage and cyber terrorism.

#### Challenges in U.S.-Russia Cooperation on Cybersecurity

Despite these instances of cooperation, there have been significant challenges in U.S.-Russia cooperation on cybersecurity. One of the main challenges is the lack of trust between the two nations. The United States has accused Russia of engaging in cyber attacks and espionage, while Russia has accused the United States of doing the same. This lack of trust has made it difficult for the two nations to work together effectively on cybersecurity issues.

Another challenge is the differing approaches to cybersecurity between the two nations. The United States has a more open and collaborative approach to cybersecurity, while Russia has a more closed and secretive approach. This has made it difficult for the two nations to share information and work together effectively.

#### Future of U.S.-Russia Cooperation on Cybersecurity

Despite these challenges, there is still potential for future cooperation between the United States and Russia on cybersecurity. The U.S.-China Law Enforcement and Cyber Security Dialogue provides a framework for continued cooperation, and there have been efforts to establish similar dialogues with other nations. Additionally, the U.S.-China Arms Control Technical Exchange Program has shown that cooperation is possible, even in areas where there may be significant differences in approach.

In the future, it will be important for the United States and Russia to continue to work together on cybersecurity issues, despite their differences. By doing so, they can better protect their own citizens and contribute to a safer and more secure global cyber environment.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between the United States and Russia in terms of foreign policy. We have examined the historical context of this relationship, including the Cold War and the collapse of the Soviet Union, and how these events have shaped current U.S. foreign policy towards Russia. We have also delved into the various factors that influence U.S. foreign policy towards Russia, such as economic interests, security concerns, and ideological differences.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of understanding the historical context of U.S.-Russia relations. The legacy of the Cold War and the collapse of the Soviet Union continue to have a significant impact on current foreign policy decisions. Additionally, it is crucial to recognize the multifaceted nature of U.S. foreign policy towards Russia, which is influenced by a variety of factors and interests.

As we continue to navigate the complexities of U.S.-Russia relations, it is essential to approach these issues with a comprehensive understanding of the historical, political, and economic factors at play. By doing so, we can better understand the motivations and actions of both the United States and Russia, and potentially work towards a more cooperative and stable relationship between these two global powers.

## Chapter: Chapter 16: U.S. Foreign Policy and China

### Introduction

The relationship between the United States and China has been a topic of great interest and debate for decades. As two of the world's largest and most influential countries, their interactions have had a significant impact on global politics, economics, and security. In this chapter, we will delve into the complexities of U.S. foreign policy towards China, examining the historical context, current dynamics, and potential future developments.

The United States and China have a long history of diplomatic relations, dating back to the 1970s when the two countries established formal diplomatic ties. Since then, the relationship has evolved significantly, with both countries playing crucial roles in shaping global affairs. The U.S. has been a major economic and military power, while China has risen to become the world's second-largest economy and a major military and technological power.

One of the key factors that have shaped U.S. foreign policy towards China is the concept of containment. This strategy, which was first implemented during the Cold War, aimed to limit the spread of communism by containing it within its existing borders. The U.S. has continued to use this strategy in its approach to China, attempting to contain its economic and military power.

However, as China's economic and military power has grown, the U.S. has faced challenges in maintaining its dominance in the Asia-Pacific region. This has led to a shift in U.S. foreign policy towards a more assertive approach, with the U.S. engaging in a strategic pivot towards the region. This pivot has been driven by the U.S.'s desire to maintain its economic and military influence in the region, as well as to counter the growing power of China.

In this chapter, we will explore the various aspects of U.S. foreign policy towards China, including economic, political, and military factors. We will also examine the impact of this relationship on global affairs and the potential future developments in this complex and ever-evolving relationship. 


# American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

## Chapter 16: U.S. Foreign Policy and China




### Subsection: 15.3c U.S.-Russia Conflict in Cyberspace

The relationship between the United States and Russia in the realm of cybersecurity has been marked by both cooperation and conflict. While the two nations have worked together to address global cyber threats, there have also been instances of cyber attacks and espionage between them. This section will explore the history of U.S.-Russia conflict in cyberspace, including notable instances of cyber attacks and the challenges that have arisen.

#### Notable Instances of U.S.-Russia Conflict in Cyberspace

One notable instance of U.S.-Russia conflict in cyberspace is the Russian interference in the 2016 United States elections. This interference, which has been described as information warfare, has been a major point of contention between the two nations. The United States has accused Russia of using cyber attacks and propaganda to influence the outcome of the election, while Russia has denied these claims.

Another notable instance of cyber conflict is the Russian cyber attacks on Ukraine. In 2014, Russia launched a series of cyber attacks on Ukraine, targeting government agencies, banks, and other critical infrastructure. These attacks were part of Russia's larger invasion of Ukraine, and they highlighted the growing threat of cyber warfare in modern conflicts.

#### Challenges in U.S.-Russia Conflict in Cyberspace

The U.S.-Russia conflict in cyberspace presents significant challenges for both nations. One of the main challenges is the difficulty in attributing cyber attacks to specific actors. With the ability to mask their identities and locations, it can be challenging to determine who is responsible for cyber attacks. This makes it difficult for the United States and Russia to respond effectively to cyber threats.

Another challenge is the lack of international norms and regulations for cyber warfare. Unlike traditional forms of warfare, there are no clear rules or guidelines for cyber warfare. This makes it difficult for the United States and Russia to navigate the complexities of cyber conflict, as there is no clear framework for addressing cyber threats.

Despite these challenges, the United States and Russia have made some progress in addressing cyber threats. The U.S.-China Arms Control Technical Exchange Program and the U.S.-China Law Enforcement and Cyber Security Dialogue have been instrumental in addressing global cyber threats. However, there is still much work to be done, and the U.S.-Russia conflict in cyberspace remains a significant concern for both nations.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between the United States and Russia in terms of foreign policy. We have discussed the historical context of this relationship, including the Cold War and the collapse of the Soviet Union, and how it has shaped current foreign policy decisions. We have also examined the various factors that influence U.S. foreign policy towards Russia, such as economic interests, security concerns, and ideological differences.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of understanding the historical context of U.S.-Russia relations. The legacy of the Cold War and the collapse of the Soviet Union has had a profound impact on the way the United States approaches Russia. It is crucial for policymakers and analysts to have a deep understanding of this history in order to effectively navigate the complexities of this relationship.

Another important aspect to consider is the role of ideology in U.S. foreign policy towards Russia. The United States has long seen itself as a beacon of democracy and capitalism, and has often used these values as a basis for its foreign policy decisions. However, as we have seen in recent years, this ideological approach has not always been effective in dealing with Russia. It is important for policymakers to be aware of the limitations of ideology in foreign policy and to consider other factors as well.

In conclusion, the relationship between the United States and Russia is a complex and ever-evolving one. It is crucial for policymakers and analysts to have a deep understanding of the historical context, economic interests, and ideological differences that shape this relationship. By doing so, we can better navigate the challenges and opportunities that lie ahead in U.S.-Russia relations.
