# American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

## Chapter 19: U.S. Foreign Policy and Russia




### Introduction

Brazil, the largest country in South America, has been a key player in the global arena for decades. Its strategic location, abundant natural resources, and growing economic power have made it a crucial partner for the United States in the region. In this chapter, we will delve into the complex relationship between the United States and Brazil, examining the historical context, key events, and current dynamics that have shaped their foreign policy interactions.

The United States and Brazil have a long history of diplomatic relations, dating back to the 19th century. However, it was not until the mid-20th century that the relationship began to take on a more significant role in global politics. The Cold War, in particular, played a pivotal role in shaping the U.S.-Brazil relationship, with both countries aligning themselves with the Western bloc.

Since then, the relationship has evolved significantly, with Brazil emerging as a major economic power and the United States viewing it as a key ally in the region. The two countries have collaborated on a range of issues, from trade and investment to security and drug trafficking. However, there have also been periods of tension and conflict, particularly over issues such as human rights and environmental policies.

In this chapter, we will explore these dynamics in detail, examining the historical context, key events, and current trends that have shaped the U.S.-Brazil relationship. We will also analyze the impact of U.S. foreign policy on Brazil, and vice versa, and discuss the future prospects for this important partnership. 




### Subsection: 19.1 U.S.-Brazil Trade Relations

The United States and Brazil have a complex and multifaceted relationship, with trade being a significant component. The two nations have been trading partners since the mid-1800s, with Brazilian coffee exports becoming an essential commodity for American markets. This trade relationship has evolved over time, with both countries playing crucial roles in each other's economies.

#### Historical Context

The early history of U.S.-Brazil trade relations can be traced back to the mid-1800s when Brazilian coffee exports became a significant commodity for American markets. This led to the establishment of American investors and merchants in Brazil, further strengthening the ties between the two nations.

In the late 19th century, the United States played a crucial role in the modernization of Brazil's economy. American capital and technology were instrumental in the development of Brazil's infrastructure, including railroads, telegraph lines, and factories. This investment not only boosted Brazil's economy but also solidified the economic ties between the two nations.

#### Current State

Today, the United States and Brazil have a bilateral trade relationship worth over $100 billion, making Brazil the United States' ninth-largest trading partner. The two nations have a diverse trade relationship, with both countries exporting and importing a wide range of goods and services.

One of the most significant aspects of U.S.-Brazil trade relations is the trade imbalance between the two nations. The United States has a significant trade deficit with Brazil, with Brazilian exports to the United States exceeding American exports to Brazil. This trade imbalance has been a source of tension between the two nations, with the United States often criticizing Brazil for its trade policies.

#### Trade Policies and Agreements

The United States and Brazil have been involved in various trade agreements, including the North American Free Trade Agreement (NAFTA) and the United States-Brazil Trade and Investment Framework Agreement. These agreements have aimed to reduce trade barriers and promote economic growth between the two nations.

However, there have been instances of trade disputes between the United States and Brazil. For example, in 2019, the United States imposed tariffs on Brazilian steel and aluminum, citing national security concerns. This move was met with strong opposition from Brazil, with the country retaliating with its own tariffs on American goods.

#### Future Prospects

Despite the trade imbalance and occasional trade disputes, the United States and Brazil continue to have a strong trade relationship. Both nations recognize the importance of trade in their economies and have been working towards strengthening their trade ties.

In recent years, there have been efforts to address the trade imbalance between the two nations. In 2019, the United States and Brazil signed a Memorandum of Understanding (MoU) to promote trade and investment between the two nations. This MoU aims to increase trade and investment flows, create jobs, and promote economic growth.

In conclusion, U.S.-Brazil trade relations have been a crucial component of their overall relationship. While there have been challenges and trade disputes, both nations recognize the importance of trade in their economies and have been working towards strengthening their trade ties. The future prospects for U.S.-Brazil trade relations look promising, with both nations committed to promoting economic growth and reducing trade barriers.





### Subsection: 19.2 U.S.-Brazil Security Cooperation

The United States and Brazil have a complex relationship when it comes to security cooperation. This relationship has evolved over time, with both nations facing unique challenges and opportunities in the realm of security.

#### Historical Context

The United States and Brazil have a long history of security cooperation, dating back to the early 20th century when the United States played a crucial role in modernizing Brazil's military. American military advisors were instrumental in training Brazilian soldiers and officers, helping to establish a strong military presence in the country.

During the Cold War, the United States and Brazil worked closely together to combat communism and other threats to regional stability. This cooperation included joint military exercises, intelligence sharing, and training programs.

#### Current State

Today, the United States and Brazil continue to cooperate on security issues, with a focus on counter-narcotics efforts, counter-terrorism, and border security. The two nations have established a Joint Task Force South, which coordinates efforts to combat drug trafficking and other transnational crimes.

In recent years, the United States has also provided significant military aid to Brazil, with a focus on modernizing the Brazilian military and improving its capabilities. This aid has included training, equipment, and technology transfers.

#### Challenges and Opportunities

Despite the strong security cooperation between the United States and Brazil, there have been challenges in this relationship. One of the main challenges has been Brazil's reluctance to actively join the War on Terror and its strong opposition to the Bush administration's Iraq War.

However, under the Lula and Rousseff administrations, Brazil has continued to work closely with the United States on security issues. This cooperation has been driven by shared concerns over drug trafficking, terrorism, and regional stability.

#### Future Prospects

Looking ahead, the United States and Brazil will continue to face challenges and opportunities in their security cooperation. As Brazil's economy and influence continue to grow, it will be important for the two nations to maintain a strong partnership in the realm of security. This partnership will be crucial in addressing the complex and evolving security threats facing both nations and the region as a whole.





### Subsection: 19.3a U.S.-Brazil Dialogue on Amazon Deforestation

The Amazon rainforest, the largest and most biodiverse tropical rainforest in the world, has been facing significant deforestation in recent years. This has been a major concern for both the United States and Brazil, given the potential environmental, economic, and social impacts of this loss.

#### Historical Context

The United States and Brazil have a long history of cooperation on environmental issues, with a particular focus on the Amazon rainforest. This cooperation has been driven by shared concerns over the loss of biodiversity, the potential impacts on climate change, and the potential loss of indigenous communities who rely on the forest for their livelihoods.

In the 1980s, the United States and Brazil established the Amazon Basin Program, a bilateral cooperation agreement aimed at addressing the environmental and social impacts of deforestation in the Amazon. This program has been instrumental in providing technical and financial support for conservation efforts in Brazil.

#### Current State

Today, the United States and Brazil continue to work closely together to address the issue of Amazon deforestation. This cooperation includes joint research and monitoring efforts, capacity building initiatives, and policy dialogue.

One of the key areas of cooperation has been the development and implementation of the Amazon Fund, a Brazilian government initiative aimed at promoting sustainable development in the Amazon region. The United States has been a major donor to this fund, providing over $1 billion in support since its inception in 2008.

#### Challenges and Opportunities

Despite the significant efforts of the United States and Brazil, Amazon deforestation continues to be a major challenge. Deforestation rates have been fluctuating in recent years, with a slight decrease in 2019 compared to 2018. However, the overall trend remains concerning, with an estimated 17% of the Amazon rainforest already lost.

There are also ongoing challenges in terms of enforcement and accountability. While there have been efforts to strengthen laws and regulations aimed at protecting the Amazon, there are still significant gaps in enforcement, particularly in remote areas.

However, there are also opportunities for further cooperation and progress. The United States and Brazil have been working together to develop and implement innovative technologies for monitoring and tracking deforestation, such as satellite imagery and remote sensing. These technologies have been instrumental in identifying areas at risk and tracking changes over time.

Furthermore, there have been efforts to promote sustainable land use practices, such as agroforestry and sustainable agriculture, as alternatives to deforestation. These efforts have been supported by the United States through technical assistance and capacity building initiatives.

In conclusion, the United States and Brazil have a long history of cooperation on Amazon deforestation, and this cooperation remains a top priority. While there are still significant challenges, there have been important steps forward, and the two nations remain committed to working together to address this critical issue.




### Subsection: 19.3b U.S.-Brazil Cooperation on Climate Change

Climate change is a global issue that requires concerted efforts from all nations. The United States and Brazil, as two of the largest and most influential countries in the world, have a crucial role to play in addressing this issue. In recent years, both countries have faced significant environmental challenges, particularly in the areas of deforestation and climate change. This has led to increased cooperation between the two nations, with a particular focus on climate change.

#### Historical Context

The United States and Brazil have a long history of cooperation on environmental issues, with a particular focus on climate change. This cooperation has been driven by shared concerns over the potential impacts of climate change on ecosystems, economies, and societies.

In the 1990s, the United States and Brazil established the Amazon Basin Program, a bilateral cooperation agreement aimed at addressing the environmental and social impacts of deforestation in the Amazon. This program has been instrumental in providing technical and financial support for conservation efforts in Brazil.

#### Current State

Today, the United States and Brazil continue to work closely together to address the issue of climate change. This cooperation includes joint research and monitoring efforts, capacity building initiatives, and policy dialogue.

One of the key areas of cooperation has been the development and implementation of the Amazon Fund, a Brazilian government initiative aimed at promoting sustainable development in the Amazon region. The United States has been a major donor to this fund, providing over $1 billion in support since its inception in 2008.

#### U.S.-Brazil Cooperation on Climate Change

Climate change is a global issue that requires concerted efforts from all nations. The United States and Brazil, as two of the largest and most influential countries in the world, have a crucial role to play in addressing this issue. In recent years, both countries have faced significant environmental challenges, particularly in the areas of deforestation and climate change. This has led to increased cooperation between the two nations, with a particular focus on climate change.

One of the key areas of cooperation has been the development and implementation of the Amazon Fund, a Brazilian government initiative aimed at promoting sustainable development in the Amazon region. The United States has been a major donor to this fund, providing over $1 billion in support since its inception in 2008. This funding has been used to support a variety of initiatives, including sustainable agriculture practices, reforestation efforts, and conservation projects.

In addition to financial support, the United States and Brazil have also collaborated on research and monitoring efforts related to climate change. This includes joint studies on the impacts of deforestation on climate change, as well as efforts to monitor and track greenhouse gas emissions in the Amazon region.

Furthermore, the two nations have also worked together to develop and implement policies aimed at reducing greenhouse gas emissions. This includes efforts to promote renewable energy sources, improve energy efficiency, and reduce deforestation.

Overall, the cooperation between the United States and Brazil on climate change has been a crucial aspect of their relationship. As both nations continue to face significant environmental challenges, this cooperation will remain a key priority in the years to come.




### Subsection: 19.3c U.S.-Brazil Partnership on Biodiversity Conservation

Biodiversity conservation is a critical aspect of environmental cooperation between the United States and Brazil. The two countries have a shared responsibility to protect and preserve their rich biodiversity, which is home to a significant portion of the world's species. This partnership is guided by the Convention on Biological Diversity, which recognizes biodiversity conservation as a common concern of humankind and an integral part of the development process.

#### Historical Context

The United States and Brazil have a long history of cooperation on biodiversity conservation. This cooperation has been driven by shared concerns over the loss of biodiversity and the potential impacts on ecosystems, economies, and societies.

In the 1990s, the United States and Brazil established the Amazon Basin Program, a bilateral cooperation agreement aimed at addressing the environmental and social impacts of deforestation in the Amazon. This program has been instrumental in providing technical and financial support for conservation efforts in Brazil.

#### Current State

Today, the United States and Brazil continue to work closely together to address the issue of biodiversity conservation. This cooperation includes joint research and monitoring efforts, capacity building initiatives, and policy dialogue.

One of the key areas of cooperation has been the development and implementation of the Amazon Fund, a Brazilian government initiative aimed at promoting sustainable development in the Amazon region. The United States has been a major donor to this fund, providing over $1 billion in support since its inception in 2008.

#### U.S.-Brazil Partnership on Biodiversity Conservation

The U.S.-Brazil partnership on biodiversity conservation is a prime example of successful international cooperation. It demonstrates the importance of shared responsibility and mutual benefit in addressing global environmental challenges. The partnership has been instrumental in preserving biodiversity in both countries and has set a model for other international partnerships.

The partnership has been particularly successful in promoting sustainable development in the Amazon region. Through the Amazon Fund, the United States and Brazil have worked together to support sustainable practices that balance economic development with environmental conservation. This has included initiatives such as sustainable agriculture, forestry, and tourism, as well as efforts to protect indigenous communities and their traditional lands.

In addition to the Amazon Fund, the U.S.-Brazil partnership on biodiversity conservation has also included efforts to protect other important ecosystems, such as the Atlantic Forest and the Cerrado. These efforts have been guided by the principles of the Convention on Biological Diversity, which emphasizes the importance of biodiversity conservation in sustainable development.

The U.S.-Brazil partnership on biodiversity conservation serves as a model for other international partnerships. It demonstrates the importance of shared responsibility and mutual benefit in addressing global environmental challenges. By working together, the United States and Brazil have been able to make significant progress in preserving their rich biodiversity and promoting sustainable development. This partnership serves as a testament to the power of international cooperation in addressing global environmental challenges.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between the United States and Brazil in terms of foreign policy. We have seen how the two countries have interacted over the years, with periods of cooperation and conflict. We have also examined the various factors that have influenced this relationship, including economic interests, political ideologies, and cultural differences.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of understanding the historical context of U.S.-Brazil relations. The two countries have a long history of interaction, dating back to the 19th century when the United States played a significant role in the independence of Brazil. This history has shaped the dynamics of their relationship, with both countries having a deep understanding of each other's history and culture.

Another important aspect to consider is the impact of U.S. foreign policy on Brazil. The United States has been a major player in Latin America, and its policies have had a significant impact on the region. Brazil, as one of the largest and most influential countries in Latin America, has been directly affected by these policies. We have seen how U.S. interventions in Brazil, such as the military coup in 1964, have had long-lasting effects on the country's political and economic landscape.

In conclusion, the relationship between the United States and Brazil is complex and multifaceted. It is shaped by a variety of factors and has been influenced by historical events. As we continue to see changes in the global political landscape, it is crucial to understand the dynamics of this relationship and its impact on both countries and the region as a whole.

## Chapter: American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will delve into the complex relationship between the United States and Mexico in terms of foreign policy. The United States and Mexico share a long and intertwined history, with a relationship that has been shaped by various political, economic, and social factors. The two countries have been neighbors for over 150 years, and their relationship has been marked by both cooperation and conflict.

The United States has been a major player in Latin America, and Mexico has been a key ally and trading partner. However, the relationship between the two countries has not always been smooth. The United States has been criticized for its interventionist policies in Latin America, with Mexico being a prime example. The U.S. has been accused of using its economic and military power to influence Mexican politics and policies, leading to tensions and conflicts between the two nations.

In this chapter, we will explore the history of U.S.-Mexico relations, including key events such as the Mexican-American War and the North American Free Trade Agreement. We will also examine the current state of the relationship between the two countries, including issues such as immigration, trade, and security. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the complex dynamics of U.S.-Mexico relations and the impact it has on both nations and the region as a whole.


# American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

## Chapter 20: U.S. Foreign Policy and Mexico




#### Conclusion

The relationship between the United States and Brazil has been a complex and multifaceted one, shaped by a variety of factors including economic interests, political ideologies, and cultural similarities. Throughout the 20th century, the United States played a significant role in shaping Brazil's political and economic landscape, often using its economic leverage to promote stability and protect its own interests. However, as Brazil's economic power and political influence have grown, the balance of power in the relationship has shifted, leading to a more equal partnership.

One of the key factors in the U.S.-Brazil relationship has been the economic interdependence between the two countries. The United States has been one of Brazil's largest trading partners, with a trade relationship that has grown significantly over the years. This economic relationship has been a source of leverage for the United States, as it has allowed it to exert pressure on Brazil to align its policies with U.S. interests. However, as Brazil's economy has grown and diversified, it has become less reliant on the United States and more able to assert its own interests.

Politically, the United States has often used its economic leverage to promote stability in Brazil. During the Cold War, the United States supported authoritarian regimes in Brazil in order to contain communism and protect its own interests. However, as Brazil transitioned to democracy in the 1980s, the United States shifted its focus to promoting democracy and human rights in the country. This has led to a more equal partnership, with both countries working together to address issues such as drug trafficking and environmental conservation.

Culturally, the United States and Brazil have a strong bond, with many shared values and interests. This has led to a close personal relationship between the two countries' leaders, with frequent visits and joint initiatives. However, there have also been tensions and disagreements, particularly on issues such as immigration and trade.

In conclusion, the relationship between the United States and Brazil has been shaped by a complex interplay of economic, political, and cultural factors. While the United States has played a significant role in shaping Brazil's history, the balance of power has shifted as Brazil's economic and political influence has grown. Moving forward, it will be important for both countries to continue working together to address shared challenges and promote mutual interests.

### Introduction

The United States has a long and complex history of involvement in Nigeria, one of the largest and most influential countries in Africa. This chapter will provide a comprehensive analysis of the U.S. foreign policy towards Nigeria, examining the historical context, key events, and current strategies.

The United States has been involved in Nigeria since the 19th century, primarily through missionary work and trade. However, it was not until the mid-20th century that the U.S. began to actively engage in foreign policy towards Nigeria. This chapter will delve into the reasons behind this shift, including the U.S.'s growing economic interests in Nigeria and its desire to contain the spread of communism in Africa.

The chapter will also explore the key events that have shaped U.S. foreign policy towards Nigeria, such as the Nigerian Civil War and the rise of oil production in the country. These events have had a significant impact on the U.S.'s approach to Nigeria, and this chapter will examine how they have influenced U.S. foreign policy decisions.

Finally, this chapter will discuss the current state of U.S. foreign policy towards Nigeria, including the U.S.'s role in addressing issues such as corruption, human rights, and economic development in the country. It will also explore potential future developments in U.S.-Nigeria relations and the implications for both countries and the region.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of U.S. foreign policy towards Nigeria, highlighting the complex and evolving nature of this relationship. By examining the historical context, key events, and current strategies, readers will gain a deeper understanding of the U.S.'s approach to Nigeria and its impact on the country and the region.




### Subsection: 20.1 U.S.-Nigeria Security Cooperation

The United States and Nigeria have a complex relationship when it comes to security cooperation. This relationship has been shaped by various factors, including the Chibok schoolgirls kidnapping, the Africa Crisis Response Initiative, and the Global Coalition to Defeat ISIS (D-ISIS).

#### Chibok Schoolgirls Kidnapping

The Chibok schoolgirls kidnapping in northern Nigeria in April 2014 sparked international outrage and brought attention to the security issues in the region. In response to this incident, the United States committed to providing assistance to Nigeria. This assistance included sending an interdisciplinary team to assist the Nigerian military, initially comprising 38 members, including two Federal Bureau of Investigation hostage specialists and several military intelligence analysts. 80 American troops were also deployed shortly afterwards.

However, there were tensions between the U.S. team and Nigerian officials, with U.S. officials complaining that Nigeria had responded too slowly in accepting and implementing the U.S.'s offer of assistance. This early stage of the mission saw the U.S. team acquiring commercial satellite imagery and flying manned intelligence, surveillance, and reconnaissance flights over Nigeria.

#### Africa Crisis Response Initiative

The Africa Crisis Response Initiative (ACRI) has been a key component of U.S.-Nigeria security cooperation. Established in 2007, ACRI has been a hub for cooperation against piracy, drug trafficking, oil theft, and border fraud in the Gulf of Guinea. Nigeria is a member of ACRI, and the U.S. and Nigeria co-hosted a virtual D-ISIS conference in October 2020.

#### Global Coalition to Defeat ISIS (D-ISIS)

Nigeria is also a member of the Global Coalition to Defeat ISIS (D-ISIS). The U.S. and Nigeria work together to combat ISIS and other terrorist groups in the region. This cooperation includes intelligence sharing, training, and joint operations.

#### Military Support

The United States provides military support to Nigeria through various programs, including the Africa Military Education Program and the Trans-Sahara Counterterrorism Partnership. In 2020, Nigeria bought over $1.2 million in defense equipment from the U.S. Additionally, a member of the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers has been stationed permanently at the Kainji Airbase in Nigeria to oversee key U.S. Africa Command projects there.

In conclusion, U.S.-Nigeria security cooperation has been shaped by various factors, including the Chibok schoolgirls kidnapping, the Africa Crisis Response Initiative, and the Global Coalition to Defeat ISIS (D-ISIS). While there have been tensions and challenges, both countries continue to work together to address security issues in the region.




### Subsection: 20.2 U.S.-Nigeria Trade Relations

The United States and Nigeria have a complex relationship when it comes to trade. This relationship has been shaped by various factors, including the Nigeria-United States Bi-National Commission, the Trade and Investment Framework Agreement, and the Africa Growth and Opportunity Act.

#### Nigeria-United States Bi-National Commission

The Nigeria-United States Bi-National Commission (BNC) is a platform for dialogue and cooperation between the two nations. It was established in 1999 and has been instrumental in promoting trade and investment between the two nations. The BNC has been a key forum for discussing trade issues and finding solutions to trade barriers.

#### Trade and Investment Framework Agreement

In 2000, Nigeria and the United States signed a Trade and Investment Framework Agreement (TIFA). This agreement provides a framework for trade and investment cooperation between the two nations. It includes provisions for market access, intellectual property rights, and investment protection. The TIFA also established the Trade Policy Dialogue, a mechanism for regular discussions on trade issues between the two nations.

#### Africa Growth and Opportunity Act

The Africa Growth and Opportunity Act (AGOA) was enacted by the United States Congress in 2000. It provides eligible African countries, including Nigeria, with preferential access to the U.S. market for certain products. This has been a significant boost for Nigeria's exports to the United States. In 2019, Nigeria was the third largest market for U.S. exports in Sub-Saharan Africa, with exports valued at $4.7 billion.

#### Trade Imbalance

Despite the growth in trade between the two nations, there has been a persistent trade imbalance in favor of the United States. In 2019, Nigeria's trade deficit with the United States was $1.4 billion. This has been a source of tension in the trade relationship between the two nations. However, efforts have been made to address this issue, including the U.S.'s commitment to increasing its exports to Nigeria's market.

In conclusion, the United States and Nigeria have a complex relationship when it comes to trade. While there have been challenges, the two nations have worked together to promote trade and investment. The Nigeria-United States Bi-National Commission, the Trade and Investment Framework Agreement, and the Africa Growth and Opportunity Act have been key instruments in this process.




### Subsection: 20.3a U.S. Criticism of Nigeria's Human Rights Record

The United States has been a vocal critic of Nigeria's human rights record, particularly in regards to police brutality and extrajudicial killings. The U.S. Department of State's annual "Country Reports on Human Rights Practices" has consistently highlighted these issues, citing numerous instances of excessive use of force by security forces, particularly the Special Anti-Robbery Squad (SARS).

#### Excessive Use of Force by Security Forces

The U.S. Department of State has consistently raised concerns about the excessive use of force by security forces in Nigeria, particularly the Special Anti-Robbery Squad (SARS). The Department's 2020 report noted that SARS officers were implicated in numerous incidents of torture, extrajudicial killings, and other human rights abuses. These abuses were often committed with impunity, as the Nigerian government failed to hold officers accountable for their actions.

#### Police Brutality and Extrajudicial Killings

The U.S. Department of State has also been critical of the Nigerian government's response to police brutality and extrajudicial killings. Despite the establishment of the Presidential Panel on Restitution for Victims of Human Rights Violations, the Department's 2020 report noted that many victims of police brutality and extrajudicial killings had not received compensation or justice. This has been a source of tension in the U.S.-Nigeria human rights dialogue.

#### U.S.-Nigeria Human Rights Dialogue

The U.S.-Nigeria human rights dialogue has been a key forum for discussing these issues. The dialogue, which is held annually, provides an opportunity for the U.S. government to raise its concerns about Nigeria's human rights record and press for improvements. However, progress has been slow, and the U.S. government has continued to express concern about the situation in Nigeria.

#### U.S. Criticism of Nigeria's Human Rights Record

The U.S. government's criticism of Nigeria's human rights record has been consistent and persistent. In addition to the annual "Country Reports on Human Rights Practices", the U.S. government has also raised these issues in bilateral discussions and public statements. This criticism has been met with varying responses from the Nigerian government, ranging from denial to promises of reform that have often failed to materialize.

#### U.S. Criticism of Nigeria's Human Rights Record

The U.S. government's criticism of Nigeria's human rights record has been a recurring theme in the U.S.-Nigeria human rights dialogue. The U.S. government has consistently raised concerns about police brutality and extrajudicial killings, as well as the failure of the Nigerian government to hold security forces accountable for their actions. This criticism has been a source of tension in the relationship between the two nations, but it has also been a catalyst for change.

The U.S. government's criticism has led to increased scrutiny of Nigeria's human rights record, both domestically and internationally. This has put pressure on the Nigerian government to address these issues and improve its human rights record. While progress has been slow, there have been some positive developments. For example, in 2020, the Nigerian government announced the disbandment of the Special Anti-Robbery Squad (SARS) in response to widespread protests over police brutality.

Despite these developments, the U.S. government continues to express concern about Nigeria's human rights record. The U.S. Department of State's 2021 "Country Reports on Human Rights Practices" again highlighted issues of police brutality and extrajudicial killings, as well as the failure of the Nigerian government to hold security forces accountable for their actions. This underscores the importance of the U.S.-Nigeria human rights dialogue in addressing these critical issues.




### Subsection: 20.3b U.S. Aid to Nigeria for Human Rights Training

The United States has been a significant provider of aid to Nigeria, particularly in the area of human rights training. This aid is part of the broader U.S. strategy to promote democracy and human rights in Nigeria, and is aimed at addressing the systemic issues that contribute to human rights abuses by security forces.

#### U.S. Aid for Human Rights Training in Nigeria

The United States has provided significant aid to Nigeria for human rights training, with a particular focus on the Special Anti-Robbery Squad (SARS). This aid is aimed at improving the professionalism and accountability of SARS officers, and at reducing the excessive use of force and human rights abuses that have been associated with the unit.

The U.S. Department of State's "Country Reports on Human Rights Practices" have consistently highlighted the need for improved human rights training for Nigerian security forces. In response to these concerns, the U.S. government has provided funding for a range of human rights training programs, including those provided by the International Service for Human Rights (ISHR).

#### International Service for Human Rights (ISHR)

The International Service for Human Rights (ISHR) is a non-governmental organization that works to promote and protect human rights around the world. The organization receives funding from a variety of sources, including major donors, trusts and foundations, law firms, and private individuals.

In Nigeria, ISHR has been a key partner in the U.S. government's efforts to improve human rights training for security forces. The organization has provided training for Nigerian security forces, with a particular focus on the Special Anti-Robbery Squad (SARS). This training has been aimed at improving the professionalism and accountability of SARS officers, and at reducing the excessive use of force and human rights abuses that have been associated with the unit.

#### U.S.-Nigeria Human Rights Dialogue

The U.S.-Nigeria human rights dialogue has been a key forum for discussing these issues. The dialogue, which is held annually, provides an opportunity for the U.S. government to raise its concerns about Nigeria's human rights record and press for improvements. However, progress has been slow, and the U.S. government has continued to express concern about the situation in Nigeria.

Despite these concerns, the U.S. government has continued to provide aid to Nigeria for human rights training, reflecting its commitment to promoting democracy and human rights in the country. This aid is part of a broader strategy to address the systemic issues that contribute to human rights abuses by security forces, and to promote accountability and professionalism among Nigerian security forces.




### Subsection: 20.3c U.S.-Nigeria Dialogue on Religious Freedom

The United States and Nigeria have a complex relationship when it comes to religious freedom. While the U.S. has been a vocal critic of Nigeria's human rights record, it has also been a significant trading partner and ally. This has led to a delicate balance in the U.S.-Nigeria dialogue on religious freedom, with the U.S. often walking a fine line between criticizing Nigeria's human rights record and maintaining strong diplomatic relations.

#### U.S.-Nigeria Dialogue on Religious Freedom

The U.S. has consistently raised concerns about religious freedom in Nigeria, particularly in the context of the country's sharia-based penal code. The U.S. government has expressed concern that this code discriminates against non-Muslims and has called for its repeal or significant reform.

In response to these concerns, the Nigerian government has argued that the code is necessary to uphold Islamic values and traditions. However, the U.S. has been unsatisfied with these arguments, and has continued to press for changes to the code.

#### U.S. Criticism of Nigeria's Human Rights Record

The U.S. has been a vocal critic of Nigeria's human rights record, particularly in regards to religious freedom. The U.S. State Department's "International Religious Freedom Report" has consistently highlighted concerns about religious freedom in Nigeria, including the use of sharia-based penal codes and the excessive use of force by security forces.

In particular, the U.S. has been critical of the Special Anti-Robbery Squad (SARS), a unit of the Nigerian police force that has been accused of human rights abuses, including excessive use of force and torture. The U.S. has provided funding for human rights training for SARS officers, in an effort to improve their professionalism and accountability.

#### U.S.-Nigeria Trade Relations

Despite the ongoing dialogue on religious freedom, the U.S. and Nigeria have maintained strong trade relations. The U.S. is Nigeria's largest trading partner, with two-way trade reaching $16 billion in 2019. This trade relationship has been a source of leverage for the U.S. in its dialogue with Nigeria on religious freedom and human rights.

However, the U.S. has also faced criticism for its own human rights record, particularly in regards to police brutality and racial inequality. This has led to some tension in the U.S-Nigeria dialogue on religious freedom, with Nigerian officials sometimes pointing to the U.S.'s own human rights issues as a way to deflect criticism.

#### Conclusion

The U.S.-Nigeria dialogue on religious freedom is a complex and ongoing process. While the U.S. has been a vocal critic of Nigeria's human rights record, it has also been a significant trading partner and ally. This has led to a delicate balance in the dialogue, with the U.S. often walking a fine line between criticizing Nigeria's human rights record and maintaining strong diplomatic relations.
